</div> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> <span class="author-timestamp" content="2019-09-25T05:54-500" itemprop="datePublished">September 25 at 5:54 PM</span> </div> <p data-elm-loc="0">House Speaker Nancy Pelosi (D-Calif.) announced Tuesday that the House would begin impeachment proceedings against President Trump, but there are many steps between the first step of launching an impeachment inquiry and the final step, which could be removing him from office.</p> <div class="inline-content inline-html" data-elm-loc="1"> <div class="pg-graphic fallback-available" The Constitution says the Senate has “the sole power to try” but does not require that a trial occur. McConnell could hold a vote to dismiss the articles.</p> <p data-elm-loc="17">If there is a trial in the Senate, Chief Justice John G. Roberts Jr. would preside. First, the president would be summoned to appear and address the charges — basically, enter a plea. If he does not appear, the Senate would operate as if the plea is not guilty.</p> <p data-elm-loc="18">During the trial, House “managers” — House lawmakers who are designated to argue the case for impeachment — outline the charges, and the president’s attorneys defend him. Both sides may call and cross-examine witnesses.</p> <p data-elm-loc="19">Johnson and Clinton were tried in the Senate. Then-Rep. Lindsey O. Graham (R-S.C.) was a manager during Clinton’s trial.</p> <div class="inline-content inline-html" data-elm-loc="20"> <div class="pg-graphic fallback-available" However, voting is done in open session. The bar is high for conviction: a two-thirds majority of the senators present.</p> <p data-elm-loc="22">If convicted of any charge, the president is removed from office and cannot pardon himself to avoid losing his position, according to the Constitution. The vice president becomes president.</p> <p data-elm-loc="23">Clinton was handily acquitted, but only one “nay” vote on each of three charges kept Johnson from being removed from office.</p> <h3 data-elm-loc="24"><b>Related stories</b></h3> <p data-elm-loc="25"><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/09/25/why-now-moments-that-moved-pelosi-house-democrats-toward-impeachment/" target="_blank">Why now?
